  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_93b43c76-c757-49a6-9b84-bf4bad74f3bd'

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer9839910452770993525"><i>basis, n.<br/><br/>There has to be a moment at the beginning when you wonder whether you're in love with the person or in love with the feeling of love itself.<br/><br/>If the moment doesn't pass, that's it―you're done. And if the moment does pass, it never goes that far. It stands in the distance, ready for whenever you want it back. Sometimes it's even there when you thought you were search</i></span>
  <span id="freeText9839910452770993525" style="display:none"><i>basis, n.<br /><br />There has to be a moment at the beginning when you wonder whether you're in love with the person or in love with the feeling of love itself.<br /><br />If the moment doesn't pass, that's it―you're done. And if the moment does pass, it never goes that far. It stands in the distance, ready for whenever you want it back. Sometimes it's even there when you thought you were searching for something else, like an escape route, or your lover's face.</i><br /><br />How does one talk about love? Do we even have the right words to describe something that can be both utterly mundane and completely transcendent, pulling us out of our everyday lives and making us feel a part of something greater than ourselves? Taking a unique approach to this problem, the nameless narrator of David Levithan's The Lover's Dictionary has constructed the story of his relationship as a dictionary. Through these short entries, he provides an intimate window into the great events and quotidian trifles of being within a couple, giving us an indelible and deeply moving portrait of love in our time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9839910452770993525" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer175815499" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10511466472841133132"><a href='http://thebookgeek.co.uk' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>People who get super creative with books are always taking a big risk, you know... writing in verse, two authors writing a POV each, and now this: a novel written like a dictionary. A series of random words from A to Z each representing something about the protagonist's most recent relationship:<br/><br/><i><b>abstraction, n.</b> <br/>Love is one kind of abstraction. And then there are those nights when I sleep alone, when I curl into a pillow that isn't you, when I hear the tiptoe sounds that aren't yours.</i><br/><br/>It's a ve</span>
  <span id="freeText10511466472841133132" style="display:none"><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>People who get super creative with books are always taking a big risk, you know... writing in verse, two authors writing a POV each, and now this: a novel written like a dictionary. A series of random words from A to Z each representing something about the protagonist's most recent relationship:<br><br><i><b>abstraction, n.</b> <br>Love is one kind of abstraction. And then there are those nights when I sleep alone, when I curl into a pillow that isn't you, when I hear the tiptoe sounds that aren't yours.</i><br><br>It's a very quick read, some pages only having one sentence on them, but I found that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/11664.David_Levithan" title="David Levithan" rel="nofollow noopener">David Levithan</a>'s creativity risk paid off here and resulted in a witty but sad tale of when love doesn't work out. I am yet to be disappointed by Levithan's writing, he has a grasp of the young adult mind that is both honest but refreshingly original. His humour is often rather crude but still hilarious, and I like how he never presents readers with the rose-tinted version of life and love. <br><br>I look forward to reading more from him in the future.<br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="10511466472841133132" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

It is his first novel for adults. This modern love story is told entirely through dictionary entries which are brief and concise having a very unusual pattern and style.   <span id="freeText15717503581019360212" style="display:none">The lover’s dictionary, David Levithan<br /><br />The Lover's Dictionary is a 2011 novel by the American author David Levithan. It is his first novel for adults. This modern love story is told entirely through dictionary entries which are brief and concise having a very unusual pattern and style. A nameless narrator tells the story of a relationship through dictionary entries. These short entries provide insight into the ups and downs of their romantic relationship, revealing the couple's problems with alcoholism and infidelity. The story does not unfold in chronological order; instead, it is arranged alphabetically by dictionary entries which give glimpses into the joys and struggles the characters face over the course of their relationship.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز سی ام ماه می سال 2016 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: فرهنگ لغات عشق؛ نویسنده: دیوید لویتان؛ مترجم سید مصطفی رضیئی؛ تهران، کوله پشتی، 1393؛ در 206ص؛ شابک 9786006687940؛ موضوع: داستانهای نویسندگان امریکایی ؛ سده 21م<br /><br />ا. شربیانی</span>

<div id="review_271701116" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/271701116" />
    <a title="K.D. Absolutely" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2156200-k-d-absolutely"><img alt="K.D. Absolutely" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1471967140p2/2156200.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/271701116?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="K.D. Absolutely" class="user" itemprop="url" name="K.D. Absolutely" href="/user/show/2156200-k-d-absolutely">K.D. Absolutely</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to K.D. by: </span>
      Angus Miranda
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2156200-k-d-absolutely?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2156200-k-d-absolutely?shelf=tfg-100">tfg-100</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer271701116" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5464309333782536342">Read this book only when you are in love or you are in love with love.<br/><br/>I was neither both when I read this in one sitting last Saturday. Then last night, I happened to catch some scenes of the Korean movie <i>Love Phobia</i> at Cinema One. Korean filmmakers have been producing excellent, i.e., very sensitive, love stories that are much attuned to Filipino’s notion of love. That’s maybe one of the reasons why we patronize not only their movies but also their many television series.<br/><br/>That movie put me in th</span>
  <span id="freeText5464309333782536342" style="display:none">Read this book only when you are in love or you are in love with love.<br /><br />I was neither both when I read this in one sitting last Saturday. Then last night, I happened to catch some scenes of the Korean movie <i>Love Phobia</i> at Cinema One. Korean filmmakers have been producing excellent, i.e., very sensitive, love stories that are much attuned to Filipino’s notion of love. That’s maybe one of the reasons why we patronize not only their movies but also their many television series.<br /><br />That movie put me in the right perspective about this book. It reminded me to love the idea of loving. Had I not seen the movie, I would have not liked this book, i.e., meaning 1-star rating. <br /><br />There are at least a couple of books about love that this could not compare to: Erich Fromm’s <i>The Art of Loving</i> for its clinical analysis of the nature of love and Alain de Botton’s <i>On Love</i> for its funny airplane cabin representation, complete with mathematical equation, of the probability of love occurring up in the air. This book, <i>The Lover’s Dictionary</i> is lame compared to the two. Even his small anecdotes on the what he thinks love is, pales in comparison with Eros Atalia’s <i>Wag Lang Di Makaraos</i> where the local author used “dagli” (short-short stories) that touches your heart as it tackles personal, social and moral everyday issues in Philippine setting. For me, Leviathan is a lazy writer. He did not even arrange the short stories in order. I thought that it would have been more interesting if he challenged himself by beginning his story with boy-meets-girl starting with letter “A” then the story (or snippets of it) transforms and blooms into a full love story that ends with separation with letter “Z.” I just felt that he could not do this so he jumped from one letter to another using one that suited his rambling scattered thoughts.<br /><br />What is this use of toothpaste cap as a proof of loving a woman? I’ve been married for 18 years and I heard this even prior to my wedding day. So, I always made sure, each day of my life for the past 18 years, that I put the cap back to the tube. Good that right after I got married, all the toothpaste manufacturers changed to snap cap (the cap does not need to part with the tube). So, I am surprised that Leviathan still used this analogy in this book. Come on, man, think of better and updated stuff to put in your book!<br /><br />But this is a book supposed to be for people who are in love or in love with love. So, who am I to dislike those people? Who am I to dislike love? Anyway, next week is another Valentine’s Day. The day reminds us the importance of love and so I rate this book with 2 stars. Meaning, this book is okay.<br /><br />But the Korean movie about a young man who constructs circles in the field to call the aliens from outer space just for his girlfriend to get well is a lot more interesting than this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5464309333782536342" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_186543371" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/186543371" />
    <a title="Monique" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4111021-monique"><img alt="Monique" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1400812804p2/4111021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/186543371?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Monique" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Monique" href="/user/show/4111021-monique">Monique</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Tintin, Lynai</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Monique by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/1552211-tina">Tina</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4111021-monique?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4111021-monique?shelf=five-stars">five-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4111021-monique?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4111021-monique?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer186543371" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3067938281019235636">I've been trying to construct a review in my head for this book all weekend, having finished reading it on Saturday morning, but no matter what I came up with, I feel that it will not fully represent the feelings I had while reading this book. To say that I <i>loved </i><b>The Lover's Dictionary</b> would be an understatement. <br/><br/>In a nutshell, <b>The Lover's Dictionary</b> is the simple love story of a couple, left unnamed by the author, told in dictionary form. Through carefully-chosen words, their love story unfurle</span>
  <span id="freeText3067938281019235636" style="display:none">I've been trying to construct a review in my head for this book all weekend, having finished reading it on Saturday morning, but no matter what I came up with, I feel that it will not fully represent the feelings I had while reading this book. To say that I <i>loved </i><b>The Lover's Dictionary</b> would be an understatement. <br /><br />In a nutshell, <b>The Lover's Dictionary</b> is the simple love story of a couple, left unnamed by the author, told in dictionary form. Through carefully-chosen words, their love story unfurled: how they first met, how their shaky relationship evolved into something more solid, from their first date up to the time they finally made the big <i>“C”</i>, the obligatory ups and downs of their relationship. And even though their story is nothing exceptional, a love story not all that different from the next boy-girl relationship there ever is, the unique manner in which their story was told gave it such an unconventional flavor and offbeat feel, and it was for this reason that I loved it to bits. <br /><br />When I first heard about this book from <a href="http://onemorepage.tinamats.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tina</a>, my curiosity was piqued right away because she mentioned that it was all about <b>wordplay</b>. I have a thing about words being given a different definition or connotation other than their original meaning; I consider the people who come up with these things to be the smartest and wittiest ones, and I admire them immensely. So when I realized that this book is a novel that was <i>all about</i> wordplay, I was hooked. Plus, when I started devouring the first few pages of the book, I knew I wasn't looking for a love story to read, not really. But when I finally closed the book with a satisfied sigh, I again realized that I haven't read a romance in a long, <i>long </i>time, and <b>The Lover's Dictionary</b> is just about perfect for the purpose. <br /><br />Another thing that I loved about the novel was the fact that I was able to relate to most of the entries than I would care to admit. (Ah, no, I will not go into personal details, sorry. :P ) There were parts that made me reminisce years past, there were entries that could very well be verbatim entries lifted from my very own journal, and there were moments when I could just <i>feel </i>the love – and the pain, too – shared by our anonymous lovers, seeing myself in their place, and it made me fall in love all over again. <br /><br />To conclude, let me share with you two of my favorite entries from the book. These made me feel shivery and fluttery inside and, well, <i>in love</i>: <br /><br /><blockquote><br />indelible, <i>adj.</i><br /><br />That first night, you took your finger and pointed to the top of my head, then traced a line between my eyes, down my nose, over my lips, my chin, my neck, to the center of my chest. It was so surprising, I knew I would never mimic it. That one gesture would be yours forever. </blockquote><br /><br />And:  <br /><br /><blockquote><br />love,<i> n.</i> <br /><br />I'm not going to even try. </blockquote><br /><br />So. Excuse me while I release another round of contented, romantic sighs. :)<br /><br />Review also posted <a href="http://bookishlittleme.attymonique.com/2011/08/lovers-dictionary.html" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3067938281019235636" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_239735507" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/239735507" />
    <a title="Megs ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5691412-megs"><img alt="Megs ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587306329p2/5691412.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/239735507?book_show_action=true">Nov 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megs ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megs ♥" href="/user/show/5691412-megs">Megs ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5691412-megs?shelf=z-2012-reads">z-2012-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5691412-megs?shelf=e-books">e-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer239735507" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13160590944691576668">I read this today, on Valentine's Day ♥, and it was a very interesting read. I love how this book explores the range of all different emotions people could ultimately experience in a relationship. I could really relate to so much of this book. This is not only a lovey-dovey story that will melt your heart. It is far more than that, and it is beautifully written.<br/><br/>The format of this book is very clever. Each page starts with a word dictionary style, and that's the format for the whole book which te</span>
  <span id="freeText13160590944691576668" style="display:none">I read this today, on Valentine's Day ♥, and it was a very interesting read. I love how this book explores the range of all different emotions people could ultimately experience in a relationship. I could really relate to so much of this book. This is not only a lovey-dovey story that will melt your heart. It is far more than that, and it is beautifully written.<br /><br />The format of this book is very clever. Each page starts with a word dictionary style, and that's the format for the whole book which tells the story of a couple. Each dictionary entry brings to light one aspect of the relationship.<br /><br />The opener:<br /><br /><blockquote><b>abberant</b>, <i>adj.</i><br />"I don't normally do ths kind of thing," you said.<br />"Neither do I." I assured you.<br /><br />Later it turned out we both had met people online before, and we had both slept with people on first dates before, and we both found ourselves falling too fast before. We comforted ourselves with what we really meant to say which was: "I don't normally feel this good about what I'm doing." </blockquote><br /><br />The story feels absolutely real and completely raw. Levithan details ,realistically, a relationship from it's lovely beginning:<br /><br /><i>“There are times when I worry that I've already lost myself. That is, that my self is so inseparable from being with you that if we were to separate, I would no longer be. I save this thought for when I feel the darkest discontent. I never meant to depend so much on someone else.” </i><br /><br />to the harsh, heartbreaking, bitter end. <br /><br />(Spoiler for language and spoiling the story a bit)<br /> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[“livid, adj.<br /><br />Fuck You for cheating on me. Fuck you for reducing it to the word cheating. As if this were a card game, and you sneaked a look at my hand. Who came up with the term cheating, anyway? A cheater, I imagine. Someone who thought liar was too harsh. Someone who thought devastator was too emotional. The same person who thought, oops, he’d gotten caught with his hand in the cookie jar. Fuck you. This isn’t about slipping yourself an extra twenty dollars of Monopoly money. These are our lives. You went and broke our lives. You are so much worse than a cheater. You killed something. And you killed it when its back was turned.”  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />There is not much you can really say about this story since it's very short (took me about an hour to read) and it's best to just be experienced yourself. The writing is fantastic. Your vocabulary will probably grow a bit. (I was happy to read this on the Nook, and be able to check a few of the words on the dictionary). The format is very unique and creative, and the whole book flows quite well. This was a book I didn't put down until it was finished.<br /><br />This Valentine's day ♥ (and any other day, really) you can enjoy this book whether you have found the love of your life or not. If you have you will probably get a wonderful feeling remembering your relationship in the early stages and those lovely first moments you shared. If you haven't you will probably feel lucky that you won't get your heart ripped out and stomped on like some people. If you are simply a person who knows the feeling of devastating heartbreak, and what to feel you're not alone check this book out.<br /><br />I only wish this would have been longer. The material in the book was 5-star material, but the pages written were half pages which makes me hesitant to recommend this book to some of my friends who don't like paying $9.99 for a book that is read in under an hour.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13160590944691576668" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

But Leviathan does something very neat here - he writes a love story as a series of dictionary entries, each highlighting some part of the relationship.   <span id="freeText12861159232865707215" style="display:none">Practically devoured this book. It reads like poetry - sparse, raw, emotional. Each word is like a caress.<br/><br/>It had me at hallo. <br/><br/>Whether serious or in jest, displaying teeth of envy, puzzlement, hurt, anger, the wonder of that special other, the peace of contentment, or the giddy feeling of love, this <i>A-Z</i> is sublime.   <span id="freeText7043070915831282796" style="display:none"><i>"The brief transcript of moments, written on the body, is so deeply satisfying to read."<br /> - <b>blemish, n.</b></i><br /><br />This is the most sensual book I've read in a long time. Perfection in its simplicity. It has brought my book mojo back. I am satiated. Deeply.<br /><br /><i>" 'I want my books to have their own shelves,' you said, and that's how I knew it would be ok to live together." 💕<br /> - <b>autonomy, n.</b> </i> <br /><br />*** 5 sighing stars ***<br /><br /><i>Shout out to Thomas whose gorgeous review piqued my interest. <div id="review_232888920" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/232888920" />
    <a title="Jenn(ifer)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/780933-jenn-ifer"><img alt="Jenn(ifer)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579713607p2/780933.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/232888920?book_show_action=true">Nov 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenn(ifer)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenn(ifer)" href="/user/show/780933-jenn-ifer">Jenn(ifer)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/780933-jenn-ifer?shelf=you-should-read-this">you-should-read-this</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/780933-jenn-ifer?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/780933-jenn-ifer?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer232888920" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15509725800822271840">**************************<br/><br/>A MUSICAL ACCOMPANIMENT: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=dXh4QQMulm8'>http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=dXh4QQ...</a><br/><br/><br/>**************************<br/><br/><b>re•view</b> [ri-vyoo] noun <br/>1. a critical article or report, as in a periodical, on a book, play, recital, or the like; critique; evaluation. <br/><br/>I really wish I had had the mental energy to review this book back when I finished it, but I just wasn’t in the right psychic place to do so at the time. I read it soon after finishing AM/PM, and it fit right in with that sort of flash-fiction vi</span>
  <span id="freeText15509725800822271840" style="display:none">**************************<br /><br />A MUSICAL ACCOMPANIMENT: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=dXh4QQMulm8">http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=dXh4QQ...</a><br /><br /><br />**************************<br /><br /><b>re•view</b> [ri-vyoo] noun <br />1. a critical article or report, as in a periodical, on a book, play, recital, or the like; critique; evaluation. <br /><br />I really wish I had had the mental energy to review this book back when I finished it, but I just wasn’t in the right psychic place to do so at the time. I read it soon after finishing AM/PM, and it fit right in with that sort of flash-fiction vibe I was gravitating toward at the time. This is a love story (duh) told in the briefest of chapters, each chapter meandering its way through the alphabet beginning with a word from the dictionary. I found myself, pen in hand, underlining all of the passages that spoke to me, all of the passages that I had <i>lived</i> in some way or another in my past. <br /><br /><i>“livid, adj. <br /><br />Fuck You for cheating on me. Fuck you for reducing it to the word cheating. As if this were a card game, and you sneaked a look at my hand. Who came up with the term cheating, anyway? A cheater, I imagine. Someone who thought liar was too harsh. Someone who thought devastator was too emotional. The same person who thought, oops, he’d gotten caught with his hand in the cookie jar. Fuck you. This isn’t about slipping yourself an extra twenty dollars of Monopoly money. These are our lives. You went and broke our lives. You are so much worse than a cheater. You killed something. And you killed it when its back was turned.”</i><br /><br />By the end, I had underlined over two-thirds of the book. It’s exhilarating when you relate to a book and walk away feeling "hey there’s someone else out there who gets it, who has been where I have been." But it can be temporarily damaging when you are reminded of all of the sadness and losses of the past.<br /><br /><i>“Ubiquitous, adj. <br />When it’s going well, the fact of it is everywhere. It’s there in the song that shuffles into your ears. It’s there in the book you’re reading. It’s there on the shelves of the store as you reach for a towel and forget about the towel. It’s there as you open the door. As you stare off into the subway, it’s what you’re looking at. You wear it on the inside of your hat. It lines your pockets. It’s the temperature. The hitch, of course, it that when it’s going badly, it’s in all the same places.”</i><br /><br />There were times when I wanted to smack the narrator to his senses. “You’re being pathetic!,” I’d internally scream. “Who are you, Jeffrey Brown? Toughen up!” But then there were times when I’d sympathize with him.<br /><br /><i>“awhile, adv. <br />I love the vagueness of words that involve time. 'It took him awhile to come back' - it could be a matter of minutes or hours, days or years. It is easy for me to say it took me awhile to know. That is about as accurate as I can get. There were sneak previews of knowing, for sure. Instances that made me feel, oh, this could be right, But the moment I shifted from a hope that needed to be proven to a certainty that would be continually challenged? There's no pinpointing that. Perhaps it never happened. Perhaps it happened while I was asleep. Most likely, there's no signal event. There's just the steady accumulation of 'awhile'.”</i><br /><br />I felt like I was reading his diary, that’s how intimate it was at times. Except someone had torn out all of the pages and shuffled them up. By the end, though, you really get a complete picture of all facets of this particular relationship. <br /><br />Love can be a glorious, painful, joyful, messy thing.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15509725800822271840" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1563370304" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10121819741630616384">⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐[9/10]<br/>⏩<b>Anachronism</b>- <i>noun</i><br/>In a story, chronological order is indispensable. What? It doesn't have to be. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/11664.David_Levithan' title='David Levithan' rel='nofollow noopener'>David Levithan</a> writes,<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>We do not divulge our histories chronologically. It’s not like we can sit each other down and say, “Tell me what happened,” and then rise from that conversation knowing everything. Most of the time, we don’t even realize that we’re dividing ourselves into clues.</b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>This is not another of those stories where you expect a happy ending. Or a sad ending. Or an <i>ending.</i></span>
  <span id="freeText10121819741630616384" style="display:none">⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐[9/10]<br>⏩<b>Anachronism</b>- <i>noun</i><br>In a story, chronological order is indispensable. What? It doesn't have to be. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/11664.David_Levithan" title="David Levithan" rel="nofollow noopener">David Levithan</a> writes,<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>We do not divulge our histories chronologically. It’s not like we can sit each other down and say, “Tell me what happened,” and then rise from that conversation knowing everything. Most of the time, we don’t even realize that we’re dividing ourselves into clues.</b>
</blockquote><br><br>This is not another of those stories where you expect a happy ending. Or a sad ending. Or an <i>ending.</i> A dictionary always ends in Z. <br><br>⏩<b>Aposiopesis-</b> <i>noun</i><br>This is one of my recent afflictions. And a prominent one at that. Happens every time I have to review a beautiful book(aesthetically and content-wise) like this one. <br><br>⏩<b>Affluent-</b> <i>adjective</i><br>Words. They look like they have been rendered forth in a niggardly fashion, but the few pages that they occupy are full of aphorisms. He writes<br><br><blockquote>
  <b> These kinds of fights can never be won — even if you’re the victor, you’ve hurt the other person, and there has to be some loss associated with that. </b>
</blockquote><br><br>⏩<b>Beguile-</b> <i>verb</i><br>It didn't take me long to get to z. I wish I hadn't gotten there sooner.<br><br>⏩<b>Bereavement-</b> <i>noun</i><br>That's what I felt when I got to Z.<br><br>⏩<b>Dictionary-</b> <i>noun</i><br>A simpleton like me, when asked to write, has to seek help. Or, when asked to read.<br>Like, <i>Concise Oxford English Dictionary</i> or <i>Merriam Webster's</i> or <i>David Levithan's Lovers Dictionary.</i> Good dictionaries are few.<br><br>⏩<b>Effusion-</b> <i>noun</i><br>Reading brilliant books brings forth ebullience which is then shortly followed by silence. <br><br>⏩<b>Frustration</b> - <i>noun</i><br>You understand the import right until that point..the crucial point where you zone out. English language has 26 alphabets and you don't have enough words.<br><br>⏩<b>Love-</b> <i>noun, verb</i><br><b>
  <blockquote>Trying to write about love is ultimately like trying to have a dictionary represent life.</blockquote>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456673853i/18265437.jpg" width="400" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>David Levithan doesn't care, though. His work is out and out tickety-boo.<br><br>⏩<b>Quote-</b> <i>noun, verb</i><br>Words stand; they won't leave even if you try to shake them off, when written by eminent people. David Levithan.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456673853i/18265438._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>I can’t help but admire your capacity for creative vengeance. And at the same time, I am afraid of it.<br><br>That’s the dilemma, isn’t it? When you’re single, there’s the sadness and joy of only me. And when you’re paired, there’s the sadness and joy of only you.</b>
</blockquote><br><br>⏩<b>Spontaneity-</b> <i>noun</i><br>You have read plenty of books. But, this one you remember..The well thought-out sequences. <br><br>⏩<b>Tantalize-</b> <i>verb</i><br>You don't know what happened. You don't know what to feel. You feel good. It's David Levithan. <br><br>⏩<b>X-</b><br><b>
  <blockquote>Doesn’t it strike you as strange that we have a letter in the alphabet that nobody uses? It represents one-twenty-sixth of the possibility of our language, and we let it languish. </blockquote>
</b><br><br>Yet, the letter symbolises the biggest gesture of goodwill man ever came up with-<br>Hugs, David Levithan, for this short but flummoxing ride! <br><br>⏩<b>Yesterday-</b> <i>noun</i><br>That's when I met you.<br><br>⏩<b>Z-</b> <i>noun</i><br>I happily lost my Zs over all of it! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456673853i/18265439.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456673853ra/18265440.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>You better look it up- <br>Here-<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456673853i/18265441._SX540_.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>No!!!!!! I mean, here-<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/books/1373898692i/11450859._UY200_.jpg" width="250" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_149476476" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/149476476" />
    <a title="Jo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2467655-jo"><img alt="Jo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596119990p2/2467655.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/149476476?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo" href="/user/show/2467655-jo">Jo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jo by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/1886642-catie">Catie</a>
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer149476476" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18309098645385588444"><blockquote><b>blemish,</b> <i>n.</i><br/>The slight acne scars. The penny-sized, penny-shaped birthmark right above your knee. The dot below your shoulder that must have been from when you had chicken pox in the third grade.<br/>The scratch on your neck- did I do that?<br/>This brief transcript of moments, written on the body, is so deeply satisfying to read.</blockquote><br/><br/>Wow, this book was gorgeous.<br/><br/>It took me about an hour to read (well, <i>technically</i> about 40 minutes... the other 20 minutes was taken up with me scrawling large chunks of this book i</span>
  <span id="freeText18309098645385588444" style="display:none"><blockquote><b>blemish,</b> <i>n.</i><br />The slight acne scars. The penny-sized, penny-shaped birthmark right above your knee. The dot below your shoulder that must have been from when you had chicken pox in the third grade.<br />The scratch on your neck- did I do that?<br />This brief transcript of moments, written on the body, is so deeply satisfying to read.</blockquote><br /><br />Wow, this book was gorgeous.<br /><br />It took me about an hour to read (well, <i>technically</i> about 40 minutes... the other 20 minutes was taken up with me scrawling large chunks of this book into my notebook, then running out of ink and trying to find a biro that worked) and I loved every second of it.<br /><br />It was funny, sweet, heart-wrenching and beautiful.<br /><br />I don't normally choose theme tunes for non-YA books but I just have to for this one.<br /><br /><a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=u7K72X4eo_s&amp;ob=av2e" rel="nofollow noopener">Teardrop by Massive Attack</a>.<br /><br />For some weird reason, I'm always reluctant to use my favourite bands/songs for the theme tunes but the line <i>"love, love is a verb, love is a doing word"</i> has been running around my mind ever since I picked this book up so I'm making the exception just once.<br /><br /><blockquote><b>yarn</b>,<i>n</i>.<br />Maybe language is kind, giving us these double meanings. Maybe it's trying to teach us a lesson, that we can always be two things at once.<br />Knit me a sweater out of your best stories. Not the day's petty injustices. Not the glimmer of a seven-eights-forgotten moment from your past. Not something that somebody said to somebody, who then told it to you. No, I want a yarn. It doesn't have to be true.</blockquote><br /><br />It's really interesting to read through my friend's reviews and see which entries they picked out as their favourites.<br /><br />I wonder what they say about us :)<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18309098645385588444" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

The next thing I know is being handed over a present of <i>our version of The Lover's Dictionary</i>. If I were to show it to you by publishing it and make a Goodreads' page of it, you'd be highly skeptical; for it contains only positive moments from the niches of me and my wife's heart.<br><br>All I can say in my defense is that there are only positive moments for both of us to write.<br><br>As far as I can remember I will only take the good memories from the original book. Those are indelible. The rest are just avoidable. I will like to remember the couple in the book as near perfect. The bad things don't last. Strong couples do.<br><br>The author does a wonderful job with the unique concept.<br><br>Who knew a story could be recited in such radiant manner as this.<br><br><i>Created ripples in our heart.</i></span>

<div id="review_307073679" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/307073679" />
    <a title="Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas"><img alt="Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567953607p2/2018505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/307073679?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas">Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=adult-fiction">adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=read-for-high-school-book-club">read-for-high-school-book-club</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer307073679" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer525585181001534742">I seriously need a word for my signature squeal.<br/><br/>No, really. Sometimes when I read books like <i>Gone With the Wind</i> or <i>Pride and Prejudice</i>, I squeal. Well-written romance tends to do that to me. <i>The Lover's Dictionary</i> did that to me.<br/><br/>Allow me to share one of my favorite entries.<br/><br/>"<b>brash</b>, <i>adj.</i><br/><br/>'I want you to spend the night,' you said. And it was definitely your phrasing that ensured it. If you had said, 'Let's have sex,' or 'Let's go to my place,' or even 'I really want you,' I'm not sure we would have </span>
  <span id="freeText525585181001534742" style="display:none">I seriously need a word for my signature squeal.<br /><br />No, really. Sometimes when I read books like <i>Gone With the Wind</i> or <i>Pride and Prejudice</i>, I squeal. Well-written romance tends to do that to me. <i>The Lover's Dictionary</i> did that to me.<br /><br />Allow me to share one of my favorite entries.<br /><br />"<b>brash</b>, <i>adj.</i><br /><br />'I want you to spend the night,' you said. And it was definitely your phrasing that ensured it. If you had said, 'Let's have sex,' or 'Let's go to my place,' or even 'I really want you,' I'm not sure we would have gone quite as far as we did. But I loved the notion that the night was mine to spend, and I immediately decided to spend it on you.'"<br /><br />If computers could record squeals and send them to others' screens and digital devices automatically, you would hear me squealing right now. <br /><br />This is my favorite book by David Levithan thus far. Its unique and addictive structure - a dictionary with alphabetized entries each serving as a short passage - was literally like nothing I've ever read before, and the romance was well-written and wonderfully realistic. Each entry supplies readers with a snapshot into a couple's romance, detailing the ups and downs, the zeniths and the nadirs. How the characters dealt with conflict or avoided it was maybe its most realistic feature, as sometimes people scream at each other until all of their anger dissipates or stay away from each other and let the tension slowly but surely build.<br /><br />And while almost nothing in life is 100% black and white, I would have liked a little more closure in the ending of this book. It did not satisfy me and I felt like because of it the story was entirely rising action with no true climax.<br /><br />However, I would recommend this short and quick read to anyone, especially those who are fans of romance. One thing I found intriguing was how while the main character was clearly male, the main character's partner never had their gender completely disclosed. There were hints, but no pronouns such as "he" or "she". In fact, by the time I finished the book I still had no idea whether the protagonist's partner was male or female, until I looked at the subjects in the front and saw "man-woman relationships." David Levithan has written several stories about gay couples, so I kind of chose to picture the book that way, and I will probably still do so. Just thought that I would point that out.<br /><br />If you're in a lonely mood or are brain-dead from exams (like, cough, me) then do yourself a favor and grab a copy of <i>The Lover's Dictionary</i>! Highly recommended.<br /><br />*cross-posted from my blog, <a href="http://thequietvoice18.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">the quiet voice</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="525585181001534742" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1539601144" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1539601144" />
    <a title="Anuradha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48159983-anuradha"><img alt="Anuradha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590872045p2/48159983.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1539601144?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anuradha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anuradha" href="/user/show/48159983-anuradha">Anuradha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">everyone who has loved someone.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48159983-anuradha?shelf=fucking-cheater">fucking-cheater</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48159983-anuradha?shelf=literary-gasm">literary-gasm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48159983-anuradha?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48159983-anuradha?shelf=literary-realism">literary-realism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48159983-anuradha?shelf=ro-ro-romance">ro-ro-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48159983-anuradha?shelf=all-da-feeeeels">all-da-feeeeels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48159983-anuradha?shelf=they-call-it-literary-fiction">they-call-it-literary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48159983-anuradha?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48159983-anuradha?shelf=i-like-em-short">i-like-em-short</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1539601144" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17983304370195565664">I nearly gave this 3.5 stars, but oh, the creativity! There's always extra points for creativity. Always. <br/><br/><b>
  <i>Trying to write about love is ultimately like trying to have a dictionary represent life. No matter how many words there are, there will never be enough.</i>
</b> [From <b>ineffable,</b> <i>adj.</i>]<br/><br/>If <i>Forest Gump</i> taught you that life is a box of chocolates, <i>The Lover's Dictionary</i> teaches you that love isn't. Using mere words, and in an extraordinarily creative diary-like format, Levithan shows everyone the di</span>
  <span id="freeText17983304370195565664" style="display:none">I nearly gave this 3.5 stars, but oh, the creativity! There's always extra points for creativity. Always. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>Trying to write about love is ultimately like trying to have a dictionary represent life. No matter how many words there are, there will never be enough.</i>
</b> [From <b>ineffable,</b> <i>adj.</i>]<br /><br />If <i>Forest Gump</i> taught you that life is a box of chocolates, <i>The Lover's Dictionary</i> teaches you that love isn't. Using mere words, and in an extraordinarily creative diary-like format, Levithan shows everyone the different sides of love - the good, the bad, and the ugly; the ups and downs; the traditions and the quirks; the earth-shattering moments, and the heart shattering ones. The nameless narrator here, defines words as they did to him in his relationship, and in doing so he captures the essence of love and loss and longing in the smallest number of words possible. He does so alphabetically, because <b>
  <i>We do not divulge our histories chronologically. It’s not like we can sit each other down and say, “Tell me what happened,” and then rise from that conversation knowing everything. Most of the time, we don’t even realize that we’re dividing ourselves into clues.</i>
</b> [From <b>circuitous,</b> <i>adj.</i>]<br /><br /><b>
  <i>I have never wanted a lover. In order to have a lover, I must go back to the root of the word. For I have never wanted a lover, but I have always wanted to love, and to be loved.<br />There is no word for the recipient of the love. There is only a word for the giver. There is the assumption that lovers come in pairs.<br />When I say, Be my lover, I don’t mean, Let’s have an affair. I don’t mean, Sleep with me. I don’t mean, Be my secret.<br />I want us to go back down to that root.<br />I want you to be the one who loves me.<br />I want to be the one who loves you.</i>
</b> [From <b>lovers,</b> <i>n.</i>]<br /><br />Love is vast and undefined and has too many nuances to it. It means different things to different people, and even to two people in the same relationship, it could be defined by different things. Building on that, Levithan uses simple words, words that we use everyday, words that mean different things to us, to build a story. A story between two lovers, lovers that you find rooting for, and at the same time, you don't. <i>The Lover's Dictionary</i> reminds me of all the indie romance movies I've enjoyed - the ones with an average, albeit intellectual man and this firecracker of a manic pixie dreamgirl. I sometimes judge movies for having this theme, other times, I revel in how commonplace and natural some of these stories seem. Because in my experience, it is only these that show love as not always rainbows and unicorns, but as trying and testing, and worth it in the end.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>love, n.<br />I’m not going to even try.</i>
</b><br />I have been in love exactly two times in my life. Both times, it ended badly. Both times, it was both our faults. It has taken me exactly 5 and 1.5 years respectively, to admit that last part to myself. The first time it ended, it was bad. It was passionate and tearful and bitter. On both sides. I though I would die. It took me a long time to get over it. The second time was ...quicker. Easier. Still heart-breaking, but I knew I'd survive. I didn't know if I had become more resilient or if it just gets easier with time. But it made me not so terrified of falling in love.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>obstinate, adj.<br />Sometimes it becomes a contest: Which is more stubborn, the love or the two arguing people caught within it?</i>
</b><br />When things got nasty between my second ex-boyfriend and me, he said it was my personality. I said it was his substance abuse. Based on the number of break-ups we had before it ended for good, I would have liked to tell myself that it was love that won, but then I'd be lying to myself. Don't get me wrong, it wasn't a toxic relationship; we were just two very different people looking for two very different things. And so along the way, love got lost. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>I am completely unposed, completely genuine. In my mind’s eye, I picture myself like that, reacting to you.</i>
</b> [From <b>guise,</b> <i>n.</i>] We put on disguises everyday, in front of friends, acquaintances, colleagues, even family. Until one day, in front of some people, we just don't, and to me, those are the people worth keeping in my life. And definitely the only people worth sharing my life with.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“Does everything have a name?”<br />The answer was no, only Ivan. Because when I bought it (the television) with Joanna, I promised her I would call it Ivan.<br />But I didn’t tell you that. Instead, I told you I’d named everything.</i>
</b> [From <b>nomenclature,</b> <i>n.</i>] One of my dearest friends in college had a habit of naming everything she owned. The air conditioner in her room, she named Dhanno. Dhanno was a little bitch if there ever was one, and simply refused to work until you softly stroked her while swearing your head off at her, preferably in Hindi. But Dhanno was part of our small family and I sometimes still miss her. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>These words are now mine, but soon they’ll be ours.</i>
</b> [From <b>epilogue,</b> <i>n.</i>] If I had a penny for every person who told me they'd include me in the dedication (or acknowledgement) for their book should they choose to write one, I'd give all the pennies away if it meant they would still dedicate it to me. I'm not trying to sound self-important here, but being a part of someone's words is as big a deal as being a part of someone's world, and I find it awfully touching.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Finally, I said, “It’s over.”<br />You started to cry, and I quickly said, “No — I mean this part is over. We have to get to the next part.”</i>
</b> [From <b>persevere,</b> <i>v.</i>] I've never realised if relationships, any relationships, not just the romantic ones, were <b>
  <i>contiguous</i>
</b>, or if we could separate them into stages or parts. I mean, is it all one giant mess of joy and sorrow and good and bad, or can you separate the good parts from the bad? The bad memories are always interspersed with the good and vice versa. Maybe that's why we persevere. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>gravity, n.<br />I imagine you saved my life. And then I wonder if I’m just imagining it.</i>
</b><br />The very first friend I ever made in college saved my life. I wasn't suicidal or anything, and it's not like I didn't think that I had a purpose either. But I was lost, and she sort of helped me centre myself. Maybe that's why, six years later, she's still the first person I turn to. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>In the end, we both want the right thing to happen, the right person to win, the right idea to prevail. We have no faith that it will, but still we want it. Neither of us has given up on anything.</i>
</b> [From <b>jaded,</b> <i>adj.</i>] "Jaded" literally means exhausted. And in today's context, I can think of no better definition for the word than this. Everyday, we wake up, hoping things will get better, but they don't, and here we are, exhausted that they don't. Day after day. Jaded. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>You were already seeing the rooms as ours, and that was enough for me.<br />Well, that and a dishwasher.</i>
</b> [From <b>broker,</b> <i>n.</i> and <i>v.</i>] I start my Master's program in 20 days. In a new city, new country, new everything. Of course, I also had to lease a new house, and in a way, my broker got me three great friends. Because when she sent the our of us that same email with that same house, we all saw those rooms as ours, and thus, friendships were born. Although, we did get broker too. A lot broker.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>misgivings, n.<br /> Last night, I got up the courage to ask you if you regretted us.<br />“There are things I miss,” you said. “But if I didn’t have you, I’d miss more.”</i>
</b><br />My ex (the second one, the more "real" one) and I remain friends, and one day, he asked me if I regretted our time together. It's a loaded question if there ever is one, and I surprised even myself by answering that I didn't. I didn't regret our time together. There were some incidents that I wish we could've handled differently. Some mistakes I wish we hadn't made. But I cherish "our time together" as a whole. And I think it made me a better person. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>I want to take back at least half the “I love you”s, because it feels safer that way.</i>
</b> [From <b>recant,</b> <i>v.</i>]<br /><b>
  <i>quintessence, n.<br />It’s the way you say thank you like you’re genuinely thankful. I have never met anyone else who does that on a regular basis.</i>
</b> <br />I truly believe that we take the words "sorry", "thank you", and "I love you", amongst others, for granted. We either say it too many times, or not enough times at all. And many times, we say it because we have to. We don't remember what these words mean anymore, or what they mean when we say it. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>If you and I really, truly wanted to change the world, we’d invent more words that started with x.</i>
</b> [From <b>x,</b> <i>n.</i>] My best friend from school and I invented a word. It was a nonsense word, and that was its essence. We could use it in any context, and its meaning could be derived from the context itself. Although it was years after we became best friends, inventing this word became a defining moment in our friendship. Each time we fought, we had a peace offering. And during the trying times, maybe this invented word saved us. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>masochist, n.<br />If there wasn’t a word for it, would we realize our masochism as much?</i>
</b><br />I have a shelf here, on Goodreads called "because I'm a masochist", and it refers to every bad book decision I make on purpose. I have never been a fan of using the word masochism in love. I mean, I am not disregarding the sexual fetish, nor the actual act, just the use of the word. Somehow makes the act seem...obligatory. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>yearning, n. and adj.<br />At the core of this desire is the belief that everything can be perfect.</i>
</b><br />I've never liked the idea of perfection. It's too complicated and boring. It's all the imperfections that make life worth it, and really, if everything were perfect, we'd all be out of jobs. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>Even if neither of us got what we wanted, we found freedom in the third choices.</i>
</b> [From <b>deadlock,</b> <i>n.</i>] My friends and I used to watch a movie almost every night during our last few weeks of college. There were so many movies we wanted to see together, so many choices, that some days, we used to ask random people to pick movies for us, and then watch them. We found solace in third choices.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Does every “I love you” deserve an “I love you too”? Does every kiss deserve a kiss back? Does every night deserve to be spent on a lover?<br />If the answer to any of these is “No,” what do we do?</i>
</b> [From <b>fraught,</b> <i>adj.</i>]<br />The first time my (second) ex told me he loved me, I said "okay". Not even thank you, okay. It wasn't that I didn't love him. I did, I just didn't know that that was the right time to say it. And I didn't want it to sound like an obligation because it wasn't. My ideal response in many of these situations is "okay", not because I want to be rude, but because I think I responding in any other manner would be either difficult or complicated, or sometimes, untruthful. Okay. And this is my contribution to the lover's dictionary.<br /><br /><b>okay,</b> <i>n.</i><br />Sometimes, it's okay to say okay. It's not a big deal at all, because sometimes, it is the perfect answer. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>BONUS:</u>
</b><br /><b>
  <i>You grabbed my hand and twirled me around, two sidewalk sweethearts. Then, very earnestly, you stopped, leaned over, and whispered, “You know, I’d get a tattoo with your name on it. Only, I want you to have the freedom to change your name if you want to.”</i>
</b> [From <b>unabashedly,</b> <i>adv.</i>]</span>
  <a data-text-id="17983304370195565664" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_review_2041098884'><a id="like_count_review_2041098884" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/2041098884?resource_type=Review"><span class="likesCount">26 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it gr-button gr-button--small" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F9279177-the-lover-s-dictionary">Like</a></span>

<div id="review_1417582425" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1417582425" />
    <a title="Mia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23106940-mia"><img alt="Mia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600049623p2/23106940.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1417582425?book_show_action=true">Oct 15, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mia" href="/user/show/23106940-mia">Mia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23106940-mia?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1417582425" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5624491495810754625"><b>love,</b> <i>n.</i><br/><br/>/ləv/<br/><br/>1. an intense feeling of deep affection.<br/><br/>2. feel a deep romantic or sexual attachment to (someone).<br/><br/>3. "...a smoke raised with the fume of sighs;<br/>Being purged, a fire sparkling in lovers' eyes;<br/>Being vexed, a sea nourished with loving tears.<br/>What is it else? A madness most discreet,<br/>A choking gall, and a preserving sweet."<br/><br/>4. not a single emotion, but an umbrella term for the entire range of emotions you experience in tandem with someone else.<br/><br/>When you're in love, you're also in hate. When </span>
  <span id="freeText5624491495810754625" style="display:none"><b>love,</b> <i>n.</i><br><br>/ləv/<br><br>1. an intense feeling of deep affection.<br><br>2. feel a deep romantic or sexual attachment to (someone).<br><br>3. "...a smoke raised with the fume of sighs;<br>Being purged, a fire sparkling in lovers' eyes;<br>Being vexed, a sea nourished with loving tears.<br>What is it else? A madness most discreet,<br>A choking gall, and a preserving sweet."<br><br>4. not a single emotion, but an umbrella term for the entire range of emotions you experience in tandem with someone else.<br><br>When you're in love, you're also in hate. When you're in love with someone, you're in fear with them. When you're in love with someone, you're in hope, in ecstasy, in bliss with them. You're in pain, in heartbreak, in heartache, in fury, in depression with them. You're in ambivalence, in annoyance, in pettiness with them. You're in redemption, in sin, in light, in dark, in beauty, in ugliness, in brilliance, in dullness with them.<br><br>Love can't be defined because it isn't just one thing. Trying to stick a set of words onto it, to put it in a box and quantify it- that's like trying to give life a single meaning, and it's the reason the word "the" has about thirteen different definitions in the dictionary. Words take on a different meaning based on technical things- context, verbiage, etc.- but also who says them, and why, and when. Whether somebody says something in earnest or dips it in the bitter liquid of sarcasm, whether their eyes sparkle when they say it or they look down, whether they're dissembling or honest, whether it's offhanded or a moment weighted with meaning.<br><br>But some words are universal, and they always feel the same- if I describe a person as incandescent, you don't need me to tell you that they're brilliant, luminous, splendiferous. You don't need those other words because you can picture that person in your mind, bright as a firework across the dark sky. But it's also a paradox because there can never be just one definition- that incandescent person looks different to everyone reading this. We all have different experiences, hopes, dreams, fears, expectations, and those colour the words we use just as much as they do our lives.<br><br>Trying to review The Lover's Dictionary is like trying to define love- it flits around the edges, slips out of your grasp, demands to be felt instead of explained. All you need to know about this book is that it's beautiful and sad and quietly luminous, short and sweet and bitter, fractured and whole at the same time. It's a paradox, just like love is- how can something we write countless songs and novels about, something we fight and murder and exact revenge for, something we agonise over and pine for and dream about, something we curse and denounce and renounce and rediscover and pray for and give and receive- how can the source of all of this be something so indeterminable, so imprecise, so hazy? How can love be this powerful force, and yet feel like a faint gossamer spiderweb clinging between two blades of grass?<br><br>I don't know. It's ridiculous to think there can be a definition for love, or a definition for anything, really. Because our lives are woven with words, and yet the words themselves are never enough.<br><br><br><br><i>Read for the 2016 Popsugar Reading Challenge: "A book that you can read in a day."</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1453132104i/17785104._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Also, as a postscript, I highly recommend checking out <a href="http://www.dictionaryofobscuresorrows.com" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dictionary of Obscure Sorrows.</a> This book put me very much in mind of it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5624491495810754625" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_264734095" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/264734095" />
    <a title="Emer (A Little Haze)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4629647-emer-a-little-haze"><img alt="Emer (A Little Haze)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589390599p2/4629647.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/264734095?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emer (A Little Haze)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emer (A Little Haze)" href="/user/show/4629647-emer-a-little-haze">Emer (A Little Haze)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11059834-the-lover-s-dictionary">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=cried-me-a-river">cried-me-a-river</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=adult-fiction">adult-fiction</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=5stars">5stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=read2020">read2020</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer264734095" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9694875258126827703">I first read The Lover’s Dictionary way back in 2011 and never thought it was a book I would return to... and yet for some reason I decided to pick it off my shelf tonight and started reading. <br/><br/>It’s laid out in the style of a dictionary with a list of words (going from A through Z) giving rise to descriptions that allude to a romantic love affair in non-chronological order. <br/><br/>And I lost myself in the words. <br/>The emotions. <br/>The happiness. The sadness. <br/>The pathos of the doomed love affair... or maybe i</span>
  <span id="freeText9694875258126827703" style="display:none">I first read The Lover’s Dictionary way back in 2011 and never thought it was a book I would return to... and yet for some reason I decided to pick it off my shelf tonight and started reading. <br /><br />It’s laid out in the style of a dictionary with a list of words (going from A through Z) giving rise to descriptions that allude to a romantic love affair in non-chronological order. <br /><br />And I lost myself in the words. <br />The emotions. <br />The happiness. The sadness. <br />The pathos of the doomed love affair... or maybe it wasn’t doomed? Maybe there was a future... but I couldn’t see it? There’s so much to interpret in this book between the short few lines yet all I could see and feel were melancholy. <br /><br />I love the narrative of this book. I loved how the timeline jumped around. I loved that the narrator and his paramour remained nameless. It helped me better inhabit their world. I projected myself into the read. <br /><br />And maybe that’s where my melancholy comes from because painful and all that the love affair was... I have always wanted a love affair like that. I know that’s a little girl’s screwed up dream of love... I always have romanticised doomed relationships. Stars that burn bright and fast and all that. <br /><br />This review makes very little sense. But this book... it spoke to me. As I read I could recall the old heartache I had when I first read this book and realised that in the years that have followed I have let it go. <br /><br />So maybe I have grown. Maybe I have learned that doomed love affairs are not the romantic ideals of my girlhood imagination and this older, wiser...and somewhat embittered version of myself has found a way to heal from what I thought could never be cured. <br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote><b>lover, n.</b><br /><br />Oh, how I hated this word. So pretentious, like it was always being translated from the French. The tint and taint of illicit, illegitimate affections. Dictionary meaning: a person having a love affair. Impermanent. Unfamilial. Inextricably linked to sex.<br /><br />I have never wanted a lover. In order to have a lover, I must go back to the root of the word. For I have never wanted a lover, but I have always wanted to love, and to be loved.<br /><br />There is no word for the recipient of the love. There is only a word for the giver. There is the assumption that lovers come in pairs.<br /><br />When I say, Be my lover, I don’t mean, Let’s have an affair. I don’t mean, Sleep with me. I don’t mean, Be my secret.<br /><br />I want us to go back down to that root.<br /><br />I want you to be the one who loves me.<br /><br />I want to be the one who loves you.</blockquote>
</i><br /><br /><i>
  <b>For more reviews and book related chat check out <a href="https://alittlehazebookblog.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">my blog</a></b>
</i></span>

This book is a dictionary containing some words and instead of explaining the meaning, it is defined with the help of a snippet from the life of two lovers. Some of them are truly beautiful, some of them not so.<br/><br/>But its a novel idea and it needs to be appreciated.</span>
