    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_126520944" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/126520944" />
    <a title="Tina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1552211-tina"><img alt="Tina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1333881094p2/1552211.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/126520944?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tina" href="/user/show/1552211-tina">Tina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1552211-tina?shelf=tfg-100">tfg-100</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1552211-tina?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1552211-tina?shelf=best-2011">best-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1552211-tina?shelf=literary-fiction">literary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1552211-tina?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1552211-tina?shelf=2013">2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer126520944" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5772286168552644164"><strong>Original post at <a href='http://onemorepage.tinamats.com/the-lovers-dictionary/' rel='nofollow noopener'>One More Page</a></strong><br/><br/>When I first heard about David Levithan's latest book, <em>
  <strong>The Lover's Dictionary,</strong>
</em> I wanted to read it only because of the clever idea behind the book. I love anything that involves wordplay. I loved the idea that this book is told using dictionary words, and for some reason, this gives me the feeling that this book has a universal feel to it, like anyone could relate to an entry here at one point. I ordered a copy off Book Depository a few weeks ago after I realize</span>
  <span id="freeText5772286168552644164" style="display:none"><strong>Original post at <a href="http://onemorepage.tinamats.com/the-lovers-dictionary/" rel="nofollow noopener">One More Page</a></strong><br /><br />When I first heard about David Levithan's latest book, <em>
  <strong>The Lover's Dictionary,</strong>
</em> I wanted to read it only because of the clever idea behind the book. I love anything that involves wordplay. I loved the idea that this book is told using dictionary words, and for some reason, this gives me the feeling that this book has a universal feel to it, like anyone could relate to an entry here at one point. I ordered a copy off Book Depository a few weeks ago after I realized that it's cheaper there, and when it finally arrived, I actually dropped the books I was reading to devour this one.<br /><br /><em>
  <strong>The Lover's Dictionary</strong>
</em> is quite easy to devour given its short, dictionary-like format. This book, as mentioned in the blurb, tells the story of an unnamed couple, written using different words from a dictionary. The narrator, who is a guy based on the entries, is a writer while the girl seemed like a wild, whimsical character who seems to have enchanted our narrator. But as their relationship goes on, it gets harder for the both of them, and we readers are left wondering if the they decide to stay together or part.<br /><br />The entries weren't written in chronological order so the timeline tends to jump from one anecdote to another, while others just seem like a sharing, or a comment on how the relationship is or how each has changed because of the relationship. It's equal parts sad and happy, a lot mushy and it tends to leave the readers pondering on what makes a relationship tick. There's something about finding common ground, which I really liked:<br /><blockquote><strong><em>akin</em>, </strong>adj.<br /><br /><em>I noticed on your profile that you said you said you loved </em>Charlotte's Web<em>. So it was something we talked about on that first date, about how much the world </em>radiant<em> sealed it for ach of us, and how the most heartbreaking moment isn't when Charlotte dies, but when it looks like all of her children will leave Wilbur, too.</em><br /><br /><em>In the long view, did it matter that we shared this? Did it matter that we both drank coffee at night and both happened to go to Barcelona the summer after our senior year? In the long view, was it such a revelation that we were both ticklish and that we both liked dogs more than cats? Really, weren't these facts just placeholders until the long view could truly assert itself?</em><br /><br /><em>We were paining by numbers, starting with the greens. Because that happened to be our favorite color. And this, we figured, had to mean something.</em></blockquote><br />Or this, about being intimidated by one another:<br /><blockquote><em><strong>daunting</strong></em><strong>, </strong>adj.<br /><br /><em>Really, we should use this more as a verb. You daunted me, and I daunted you. Or would it be that I was daunted by you and you were daunted by me? That sounds better. it daunted me that you were so beautiful, that you were so ate ease in social situations, as if every room was heliotropic, with you at the center. And I guess it daunted you that I had so many more friends than you, that I could put words together like this, on paper, and could sometimes conjure a certain sense out of things.</em><br /><br /><em>The key is to never recognize these imbalances. To not let the dauntingness daunt us.</em></blockquote><br />I'm pretty sure the story the authors intended for the characters here is not the same for everyone, but I think everyone who's ever loved will find that they are able to relate to one or two or more entries in <em>
  <strong>The Lover's Dictionary</strong>
</em>. This makes the book very rereadable, especially in random -- just pick it up, open to a page and read. This book also makes me wonder: if I were to make a dictionary of my own love life, what words would I use?<br /><br />But alas, my own love life is still nonexistent. That fact made me a bit distant to the novel, because I can't relate. Not yet, anyway. However, <em>
  <strong>The Lover's Dictionary</strong>
</em> affirms things that I know, based from stories, reading and yes, even experiences (the proper place to elaborate on this is on my <a title="tinamats.com" href="http://www.tinamats.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">personal blog</a> :P): relationships are messy, it takes a lot of work and it would hurt both parties a lot...but allow me to believe that even so, relationships can be beautiful at the same time. :)<br /><br />Whether you're a romantic or not, I recommend <em>
  <strong>The Lover's Dictionary</strong>
</em> by David Levithan. I'm sure you'll find a bit of yourself in one of the entries in this dictionary.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5772286168552644164" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

Everything else will be measured against it.”</i><br><br>Whenever I finish a David Levithan book, I find myself measuring other authors against him. Authors who I truly enjoy and would normally get recommended get thrown to the wayside so I can tell my friends to read Levithan instead. (Especially <i>Two Boys Kissing</i>. Drop whatever you are reading and go read <i>Two Boys Kissing</i>.)<br><br><i>“No matter how many words there are, there will never be enough.”</i><br><br>I am so enamored with Levithan’s writing that I am consciously spacing out his books and not allowing myself to consume them all because I know the above quote will hold true.<br><br>In an effort to avoid being sued by the author for republishing his work in its entirety while desperately attempting to convey my feelings in this review, I’m throwing in the towel and just telling you to read <i>The Lover’s Dictionary</i>. And then read everything else by David Levithan (even <i>Every Day</i>, which I didn’t much care for). <br><br>Oh, and one more thing. We should invent more words that begin with X.<br></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1029810616" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9309454976282677442">I gravitate towards this book quite a lot and this has been my forth year reading it in a row. I suppose it's because Levithan has the same thoughts as I when it comes to certain themes and I just want to check whether my opinion has changed. This time I could actually experience it from the perspective of someone who lived through some of the situations that are described in this book and I found it to be even more relatable. <br/><br/>Also, fun fact, since the names of the main characters aren't mention</span>
  <span id="freeText9309454976282677442" style="display:none">I gravitate towards this book quite a lot and this has been my forth year reading it in a row. I suppose it's because Levithan has the same thoughts as I when it comes to certain themes and I just want to check whether my opinion has changed. This time I could actually experience it from the perspective of someone who lived through some of the situations that are described in this book and I found it to be even more relatable. <br /><br />Also, fun fact, since the names of the main characters aren't mentioned and the whole book is written in second person, you can read it both as a male-female relationship story as well as a male-male one. I only picked up on that on this reread, since every previous time I imagined the love interest as a girl, even though there weren't really any gender markers that could have given it away. </span>

<div id="review_2673947795" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2673947795" />
    <a title="Karima chermiti" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42944800-karima-chermiti"><img alt="Karima chermiti" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521752993p2/42944800.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2673947795?book_show_action=true">Jan 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karima chermiti" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karima chermiti" href="/user/show/42944800-karima-chermiti">Karima chermiti</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007377992" href="/book/show/11450859-the-lover-s-dictionary">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42944800-karima-chermiti?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42944800-karima-chermiti?shelf=adult_fiction">adult_fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42944800-karima-chermiti?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42944800-karima-chermiti?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42944800-karima-chermiti?shelf=contemporary-romance-books">contemporary-romance-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42944800-karima-chermiti?shelf=readathons_books">readathons_books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2673947795" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12234535941746389914"><br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Trying to write about love is ultimately like trying to have a dictionary represent life. No matter how many words there are, there will never be enough. </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><i>The lover’s dictionary</i> by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/11664.David_Levithan' rel='nofollow noopener'>David Levithan</a> is a book with great concept and great execution that gives it originality and something unfamiliar. At the same time, it doesn’t lack in terms of depths and emotions yet it certainly suffers when it comes to plot and characters development.<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/11664.David_Levithan' rel='nofollow noopener'>David Levithan</a> attempts in his novel to delve deep i</span>
  <span id="freeText12234535941746389914" style="display:none"><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Trying to write about love is ultimately like trying to have a dictionary represent life. No matter how many words there are, there will never be enough. </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><i>The lover’s dictionary</i> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/11664.David_Levithan" rel="nofollow noopener">David Levithan</a> is a book with great concept and great execution that gives it originality and something unfamiliar. At the same time, it doesn’t lack in terms of depths and emotions yet it certainly suffers when it comes to plot and characters development.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/11664.David_Levithan" rel="nofollow noopener">David Levithan</a> attempts in his novel to delve deep into a relationship between two lovers from their first dates to their moments of doubts and anger going through all the stages of meeting someone from getting to know them to getting attached and falling in love to feeling trapped and scared coming to the moment when you either go further or just let it go.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>It’s always something we have to negotiate — the fact that my parents are happy, and yours have never been. I have something to live up to, and if I fail, I still have a family to welcome me home. You have a storyline to rewrite, and a lack of faith that it can ever be done. </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Told in this creative format where the author takes random words going from A to Z and writing a tiny vignette for each chosen word to make us see something about the love the two characters shares and the struggle they go through with trying to protect their relationship and themselves for what could happen. At times, you feel like the two characters are made for each other and at others you feel it is best if they call it quit but I guess that’s the reality of relationships, the ups and downs and all of that.<br /><br />Vulnerable, creative and effective, <i>The lover’s dictionary</i> is a great story that could fit any two people; the fact that we don’t know that much about the characters, we don’t even know the name of the one telling the story lakes it actually easily for anyone to see his story through their story. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Nights when I need to sleep and you can’t. Days when I want to talk and you won’t. Hours when every noise you make interferes with my silence. Weeks when there is a buzzing in the air, and we both pretend we don’t hear it. </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />But, at the same time it’s really hard to connect with characters you know nothing about, yeah, we get bits and pieces here and there but by the end of the book, they still feel like complete strangers to me. Also the story has no plot whatsoever, even the vignettes are written in a non-linear way so you kind of feel lost at times and some of them felt repetitive to me.<br /><br />I don’t know about other people who read the book, but this is more of a sober and candid interpretation of love story than a cute one, <b>There’s mention of cheating and hinting at one of the characters having problems with alcohol so trigger warning for these two topics, also, there is mention of bullying and an incident when someone is made fun of using the fact that he’s overweight so keep those in mind while reading the book</b>. I think if it wasn’t for that incident, I would gave the book 4 stars but I can’t turn a blind eye to it, it doesn’t matter if the person is a good human or not, it’s never okay to make fun of people for their appearances. <br /><br />Compulsively readable with an honest insight to love and relationships, <i>The lover’s dictionary</i> offers us a new way to look at the bonds we share with our partners.<br /> <br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Sometimes desire is air; sometimes desire is liquid. And every now and then, when everything else is air and liquid, desire solidifies, and the body is the magnet that draws its weight. </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>***********************************</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />#<a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCax5iInFtxgYeqG6MKhTPJg" rel="nofollow noopener">Winter Biannual Bibliothon</a> Day 3, Book 3</span>
  <a data-text-id="12234535941746389914" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Mimi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2490110-mimi"><img alt="Mimi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1424631975p2/2490110.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1142783639?book_show_action=true">Dec 26, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mimi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mimi" href="/user/show/2490110-mimi">Mimi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2490110-mimi?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2490110-mimi?shelf=contemporary-fiction">contemporary-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1142783639" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer615034188924990612">It's been a long time since a book made me cry. This book didn't make me cry. It just reminded me that I haven't cried over fiction since <em>Charlotte's Web.</em><br/><br/>Simply put, this book is an interesting way to tell a modern love story (from a writer's perspective), and an interesting way to see vocabulary words in new ways (from a reader's) while you watch different aspects of a relationship come together, stay together, fall apart, and then go through these stages again. If you're not currently in love </span>
  <span id="freeText615034188924990612" style="display:none">It's been a long time since a book made me cry. This book didn't make me cry. It just reminded me that I haven't cried over fiction since <em>Charlotte's Web.</em><br /><br />Simply put, this book is an interesting way to tell a modern love story (from a writer's perspective), and an interesting way to see vocabulary words in new ways (from a reader's) while you watch different aspects of a relationship come together, stay together, fall apart, and then go through these stages again. If you're not currently in love or involved with someone special, this book might seem a tad overbearing and overwrought, rather than meaningful or fascinating. Three guesses which camp I'm in. :D<br /><br />Clearly I'm not the right audience for this book and I might've picked it up at an inconvenient time which is too bad because I do like the way David Levithan uses words. He has a nice way with them. His prose is simple, light, smooth, and occasionally a line or two can pack a punch when the story calls for it. And there's clever use of biting humor that's just shy of passive-aggression. Just the way I like my contemporary fiction to be, so it really is too bad that this book and I didn't hit it off. Maybe if I'd read it 10 years ago, when I'd been a bit more idealistic and optimistic about romantic outcomes, these lovely words and phrases might've had an impact. Now? Now processing these things takes me back to that time years ago and I get to reminisce and... and that's it. It does nothing more for me now, which is too bad.<br /><br />Clearly I'm not the right audience for this book, but that doesn't mean it isn't well written, not to mention clean and thoughtfully compartmentalized. It's as clean and compartmentalized as relationships are messy and overwhelming. The whole thing is lovingly crafted, I think, which shows in the care Levithan has for his word choices. I can go on about it, but I'll just show you instead.<br /><br />[images posted, along with review at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://covers2covers.wordpress.com/2014/12/28/review-the-lovers-dictionary/">https://covers2covers.wordpress.com/2...</a>]<br /><br />Levithan puts words together with such ease. I really wish I could've liked this book more. Maybe 10 years from now I'll read it again at a different place in my life and will like it more.<br /><br /><br />On a semi-related note, I saw Gone Girl over the weekend. Didn't like the book, but thought the movie was decent, with the exception of Ben Affleck who will always be Ben Affleck in whatever role he tries to bring to life. Some of us are just blessed/cursed to forever be ourselves, I suppose.<br /><br />Anyhow. As I was going over review notes I took for <em>The Lover's Dictionary</em>, it dawned on me that this book is the life Nick and Amy Dunne must've had before they married and everything went to hell. In this life before marriage, both Nick and Amy seem happier with themselves and each other, and that's what the tone of <em>Dictionary</em> reminds me of most, the easy pleasantry of dating. For more similarities, I'd point to the unnamed narrator and Nick Dunne sharing a similar POV; both are usually sitting on the sidelines as they watch and react to things happening to them. Instead of acting upon these things or taking control as they spiral out of their grasps, they watch and then react.<br /><br />The moment I realized the unnamed narrator and Nick Dunne are one and the same and that the person they're dating is Amy was this line:<br /><blockquote>I can't help but admire your capacity for creative vengeance. And at the same time, I am afraid of it.</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="615034188924990612" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_136698036" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/136698036" />
    <a title="Isamlq" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4016030-isamlq"><img alt="Isamlq" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483590305p2/4016030.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/136698036?book_show_action=true">Dec 27, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Isamlq" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Isamlq" href="/user/show/4016030-isamlq">Isamlq</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer136698036" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1095147475351520565">Full disclosure, I might have blinders on where this author is concerned because every book of his that I've read, I've really enjoyed... (Nick and Norah, Dash and Lily, the Will Graysons even Naomi and Ely were all wonderful reads!) With Lover's Dictionary, I didn't know what I was getting into. But good golly, that was different... and refreshing! <br/><br/>It tackled what's familiar from all the possible angles. One need not strain one's imagination to see how a word applied, because it just DID. Each </span>
  <span id="freeText1095147475351520565" style="display:none">Full disclosure, I might have blinders on where this author is concerned because every book of his that I've read, I've really enjoyed... (Nick and Norah, Dash and Lily, the Will Graysons even Naomi and Ely were all wonderful reads!) With Lover's Dictionary, I didn't know what I was getting into. But good golly, that was different... and refreshing! <br /><br />It tackled what's familiar from all the possible angles. One need not strain one's imagination to see how a word applied, because it just DID. Each entry showed a different facet, a different stage of being in a relationship. Tina uses the phrase <b>word play</b> to describe it. And indeed it was as Levithan's reduces it to its essentials~ sometimes hitting it square on the end, other times oversimplifying matters, but mostly coming across as accurate and humorous. <br /><br />Succintly putting each aspect/facet/stage of the experience into a word, <b>one word.</b> I thought <b>Lover's Dictionary</b> SMART, FUNNY at times, but definitely DIFFERENT. Is it gimmicky? Is it cutesy? Not at all! I've grown used to boy-girl headoverheels/ troublerunsdeep stories, this slim volume is none of those things *thank gosh!* It hit aspects of relationships head on. I really enjoyed it!<br /><br /><b>4/5</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="1095147475351520565" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_169570285" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/169570285" />
    <a title="Alyssa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2753251-alyssa"><img alt="Alyssa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1369004887p2/2753251.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/169570285?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alyssa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alyssa" href="/user/show/2753251-alyssa">Alyssa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Readers who appreciate lyrical prose</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2753251-alyssa?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2753251-alyssa?shelf=get-with-library">get-with-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2753251-alyssa?shelf=reccomended">reccomended</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2753251-alyssa?shelf=highly-anticipated">highly-anticipated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2753251-alyssa?shelf=really-excited-for">really-excited-for</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2753251-alyssa?shelf=2012-read">2012-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2753251-alyssa?shelf=i-love-this-cover">i-love-this-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2753251-alyssa?shelf=adult-romance">adult-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer169570285" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5037553224823074732"><i>The Lover’s Dictionary</i> is my first Levithan book, but it definitely won’t be my last. I mean, when an author can come up with this,<br/><br/><blockquote><b>juxtaposition</b>, <i>n</i>.<br/><br/>It scares me how hard it is to remember life before you. I can’t even make the comparisons anymore, because my memories of that time have all the depth of a photograph. It seems foolish to play games of <i>better</i> or <i>worse</i>. It’s simply a matter of <i>is</i> and <i>is no longer.</i></blockquote><br/><br/>and later this,<br/><br/><blockquote><b>lover</b>, <i>n</i>.<br/><br/>I have never wanted a lover. In order to have a lover, I must go</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText5037553224823074732" style="display:none"><i>The Lover’s Dictionary</i> is my first Levithan book, but it definitely won’t be my last. I mean, when an author can come up with this,<br /><br /><blockquote><b>juxtaposition</b>, <i>n</i>.<br /><br />It scares me how hard it is to remember life before you. I can’t even make the comparisons anymore, because my memories of that time have all the depth of a photograph. It seems foolish to play games of <i>better</i> or <i>worse</i>. It’s simply a matter of <i>is</i> and <i>is no longer.</i></blockquote><br /><br />and later this,<br /><br /><blockquote><b>lover</b>, <i>n</i>.<br /><br />I have never wanted a lover. In order to have a lover, I must go back to the root of the word. For I have never wanted a lover, but I have always wanted to love, and to be loved.<br /><br />There is no word for the recipient of the love. There is only a word for the giver. There is the assumption that lovers come in pairs.<br /><br />When I say, <i>Be my lover</i>, I don’t mean, <i>Let’s have an affair.</i> I don’t mean, <i>Sleep with me</i>. I don’t mean, <i>Be my secret</i>.<br /><br />I want us to go back down to that root.<br /><br />I want you to be the one who loves me.<br /><br />I want to be the one who loves you.</blockquote><br /><br />why wouldn’t one want to read more?<br /><br /><b>3.5 stars</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="5037553224823074732" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zL86frIwro5+NpBxmKzvk0yE8I6p0SznraUt0kiY1erSlO8A0vF7Icr62vCaVsoJ6cMpYXtLk8sJtu7EPJLiEg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('UMfwkVmAjK9+e2qQtjgO6Dkfbq3juCCgS01uuQiH7mNO7CXvOUFZAMq3IBG0witynFi3QjEin4zvXq2vfI3Zmw==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer307541033844632201">David Levithan (born 1972) is an American children's book editor and award-winning author. He published his first YA book,<i> Boy Meets Boy</i>, in 2003. Levithan is also the founding editor of PUSH, a Young Adult imprint of Scholastic Press.<br/><br/></span>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/12922551-the-lover-s-dictionary">Quotes from The Lover&#39;s Dicti...</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;It was a mistake," you said. But the cruel thing was, it felt like the mistake was mine, for trusting you.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/365376-it-was-a-mistake-you-said-but-the-cruel-thing">3155 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;livid, <i>adj.</i><br /><br />Fuck You for cheating on me. Fuck you for reducing it to the word cheating. As if this were a card game, and you sneaked a look at my hand. Who came up with the term <i>cheating,</i> anyway? A cheater, I imagine. Someone who thought <i>liar</i> was too harsh. Someone who thought <i>devastator</i> was too emotional. The same person who thought, oops, he’d gotten <i>caught with his hand in the cookie jar.</i> Fuck you. This isn’t about slipping yourself an extra twenty dollars of Monopoly money. These are our lives. You went and broke our lives. You are so much worse than a cheater. You killed something. And you killed it when its back was turned.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/345798-livid-adj-fuck-you-for-cheating-on-me-fuck-you">2299 likes</a>
